## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Population Ecology
**Analysis**: This task is about modeling population growth rate in relation to time and population size, which is a fundamental concept in population ecology.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Logistic growth: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) (simple population growth model)
- Verhulst logistic equation: dP/dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P**2 (modification of logistic growth with competition)
- Gompertz growth equation: dP/dt = c0 * P * ln(c1 / P) (growth model with saturation and nonlinearity)
- Ricker growth equation: dP/dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * (c2 - P)) (nonlinear growth model with predation or resource competition)
- Malthusian growth model: dP/dt = c0 * P (exponential growth model without saturation or limitation)
- Pearl-Verhulst logistic model: dP/dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (c2 + P) (generalized logistic model with nonlinear carrying capacity)
- Differential equation of population growth: dP/dt = c0 * P * f(P / c1) (nonlinear population growth model with functional response)
- Exponential growth with scaling: dP/dt = c0 * P / (c1 + P) (scaled exponential growth model with limit at zero)
- Power-law population growth: dP/dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear population growth model with arbitrary growth rate)
- Weibull population growth: dP/dt = c0 * P**c1 * exp(-c2 * (t - c3)) (population growth model with time-varying growth rate)
- Gaussian distribution of population growth: dP/dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * (t - c2)**2 / c3) (population growth model with stochasticity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Population growth → Exponential or logistic growth patterns
- Population oscillation → Rational or polynomial growth patterns with oscillatory terms
- Population saturation → Sigmoidal growth patterns with saturation limits
- Population competition → Nonlinear growth patterns with competitive interactions
- Population stochasticity → Gaussian or exponential growth patterns with stochastic terms
- Population time-series analysis → Periodic or aperiodic growth patterns with time-series analysis
- Population model scaling → Scaled exponential or logistic growth patterns with scaling parameters
- Population growth delay → Differential equations with time-varying growth rates
- Population feedback → Nonlinear growth patterns with feedback mechanisms
- Population optimization → Growth patterns with optimal resource allocation
